<div id="review_1298504062" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1298504062" />
    <a title="aPriL does feral sometimes " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes"><img alt="aPriL does feral sometimes " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478243665p2/3409532.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1298504062?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="aPriL does feral sometimes " class="user" itemprop="url" name="aPriL does feral sometimes " href="/user/show/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes">aPriL does feral sometimes </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780553903102" href="/book/show/7038212-in-the-night-garden">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=literary">literary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=magical-drama">magical-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=metafiction">metafiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1298504062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1664508806655850447">It took millennia for the stories to be collected that eventually became the fairy tales we know: Grimm's Fairy Tales, The Eddas, One Thousand and One Nights. The unknown authors of these famous stories have been many, passing down oral tales for generations.<br/><br/>Now, Catherynne Valente has created an epic collection of new dark fairy tales (this anthology contains two books of interlocking stories, as does the sequel), which not only have the feel and sound of ancient myths and fantasy stories, they</span>
  <span id="freeText1664508806655850447" style="display:none">It took millennia for the stories to be collected that eventually became the fairy tales we know: Grimm's Fairy Tales, The Eddas, One Thousand and One Nights. The unknown authors of these famous stories have been many, passing down oral tales for generations.<br /><br />Now, Catherynne Valente has created an epic collection of new dark fairy tales (this anthology contains two books of interlocking stories, as does the sequel), which not only have the feel and sound of ancient myths and fantasy stories, they are full of energy, adventure, buckets of blood, amputated and mutated body parts, magic, gods, creation myths, unjust murder, evil stepmothers and sadistic kings, vengeful witches, greedy wizards, terrible enchantments, disgusting metamorphoses, forced servitude and bad marriages, ugly monsters, and yes, abused and miserable orphans.<br /><br />It didn't take her millennia, and these tales are entirely her own creation, although the stories are so amazing it seems impossible they hatched from one imagination. Each chapter introduces a character, who then tells a story introducing a character, who then tells a story introducing a character, who then tells a story introducing a character, who then tells a story introducing a character...and so on. Each chapter is short.<br /><br />The language of the book is the most poetic, creative, inventive flow of words I have <i>ever</i> read in my life! The imaginary creatures in this 'ancient' fantasy world of a magical past will take over your daydreams. There are gorgeous illustrations as well - you will want to get the print version. <br /><br />An excerpt from "The Book of the Steppe, the "Prelude":<br /><br />""On an evening, when I was a very small child, an old woman came to the great silver gate, and twisting her hands among the rose roots told me this: I was not born with this mark. A spirit came into my cradle on the seventh day of the seventh month of my life, and while my mother slept in her snow white bed, the spirit touched my face, and left there many tales and spells, like the tattoos of sailors. The verses and songs were so great in number and so closely written that they appeared as one long, unbroken streak of jet on my eyelids. But they are the words of the river and the marsh, the lake and the wind. Together they make a great magic, and when the tales are all read out, and heard end to shining end, to the last syllable, the spirit will return and judge me.""<br /><br />From the chapter "The Horsewoman's Tale":<br /><br />"Now, the holes were up and walking around like you and me by this time, and one, roughly in the shape of a Rider, climbed over the Mare and she became full, as full and huge as a horse the size of everything, can be, until she foaled the whole world in a rush of light and milk and black, black blood from the most secret depths of the sky. The grass and the rivers and the stones and women and horses and more Stars and men and clouds and birds and trees came dancing through the afterbirth of the Mare, and swam happily in her milk and stopped up her secret blood, and the world was made, and the oceans washed the shore, and the Mare went cantering into the corners of herself, which just barely showed through the burning field of her Stars, and lay in a pasture neither you nor I could guess at, and chewed her favorite Grass-Stars in peace."<br /><br />From "The Wolf's Tale"<br /><br />"The Manikarnika were seven sisters, and when they were gnawed from the flesh of the Mare, they were Stones. Jade, Granite and Opal, Garnet and Shale and Iron Ore and little Diamond, pale as a milk-soaked paw."<br /><br />From "The Witch's Tale, Continued":<br /><br />"Slowly, Aerie changed. Her feet warped with moon-colored light and seemed to melt, her arms flattened like sheets of paper without ink. Feathers grew like silken hair on her body, first the curling down and then the strong gray feathers of flight, tipped black at the edges, the color of silver thread spinning on a crystal wheel. Her mouth silent, as if in wonder at herself, bent into a graceful beak, which snapped in a kind of awe at the empty air."<br /><br />From "The Tale of the Prince and the Goose, Continued":<br /><br />"The Leucrotta is a terrible beast who lives in the Dismal Marshes. He is the color of clotted blood, part stag and part horse, of a size that dwarfs both, a mouth that stretches ear to ear, and instead of teeth it has twin rows of solid bone. It is very fearsome, I assure you."<br /><br />For the literary reader who loves writing, this book will cause said gentle reader to faint with pleasure. I recommend taking time with this, and the sequel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/547448.In_the_Cities_of_Coin_and_Spice__The_Orphan_s_Tales___2_" title="In the Cities of Coin and Spice (The Orphan's Tales, #2) by Catherynne M. Valente" rel="nofollow noopener">In the Cities of Coin and Spice</a> reading a few chapters a day. Do not think something is amiss if you must reread stories to keep track of the flow of stories - there is almost no plot other than adventures, entertainment and the frequent disappointment of hopeful aspiration and dismal fate. They are deeply metafictional with explicit echoes of actual past myths from many cultures around our world. But these are dark ugly tales, gentle reader, not for the eyes of those who prefer happy endings or romances.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="1664508806655850447" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_20803721" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20803721" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/821374-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1201283337p2/821374.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20803721?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/821374-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/821374-nicole?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20803721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12806349164355049953">The tales told to the young Prince come from the tattoos inked on the skin of a young woman. These same strange tattoos that are keeping her isolated from the rest of the sultan's household, make her seem fascinating to the prince. Each night he sneaks out to meet with her in the Sultan's gardens.<br/><br/>This book is two series of interwoven, short, personal tales told from the tattoos. Tales that ultimately braid together. Like Chaucer's Canterbury Tales there is a series of people's pilgrimages told i</span>
  <span id="freeText12806349164355049953" style="display:none">The tales told to the young Prince come from the tattoos inked on the skin of a young woman. These same strange tattoos that are keeping her isolated from the rest of the sultan's household, make her seem fascinating to the prince. Each night he sneaks out to meet with her in the Sultan's gardens.<br /><br />This book is two series of interwoven, short, personal tales told from the tattoos. Tales that ultimately braid together. Like Chaucer's Canterbury Tales there is a series of people's pilgrimages told in first person. The stories are intermittent and interspersed but linear despite their interrupted telling. Although the stories are being related in first person by various people they are really told that way by one girl to one boy. He is escaping to bright visions of the larger world adults live in. She is seeking acceptance in any world.<br />I began reading this book and immediately was repelled by the awkward and repeated use of overwrought similes. Every thing is like something else, this is arresting and distracts from the flow. The first few tales continued in this fashion but then the descriptive style became more varied and less self consciously dramatic. My least favorite description that irks me still was "desultory eyes". How do a pair of eyes lack consistency do they move disjointedly? The only way I could conceive of this fitting is if they wandered in differing directions with disconnected focus but this did not seem to be the point being made in the context. <br />I kept thinking I would put this book down but I found myself drawn back to the complexity of the telling even if I did skim passages as soon as they threatened an excess of difficult descriptions.<br />This book missed being very good by an excessive verbosity and awkward English but despite this the story's contents are worth the time to read. Her creatures were not just relating good stories but also help us look at normal behavior and why it is desirable or not. How any individual's goals could influence disparate lives. <br />I will read the sequel to see where this author goes with her ingenious, metaphorical monsters and her various humans. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12806349164355049953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2120343931" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2120343931" />
    <a title="YouKneeK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek"><img alt="YouKneeK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386369592p2/25923230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2120343931?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YouKneeK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YouKneeK" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek">YouKneeK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6465668-in-the-night-garden">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2120343931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17960570172398619578">I thought this was a very clever and unique book. At least, I’ve never read anything like it. It tells a lot of stories, I couldn’t say how many, but definitely more than a dozen. However, this is <i>not</i> an anthology. It’s layer upon layer upon layer of related stories nested inside each other. <br/><br/>The framing story is about a lonely girl who people shun because they believe she’s a demon. A curious boy approaches her and, over the course of a few days, she tells him two stories. Each of the two storie</span>
  <span id="freeText17960570172398619578" style="display:none">I thought this was a very clever and unique book. At least, I’ve never read anything like it. It tells a lot of stories, I couldn’t say how many, but definitely more than a dozen. However, this is <i>not</i> an anthology. It’s layer upon layer upon layer of related stories nested inside each other. <br /><br />The framing story is about a lonely girl who people shun because they believe she’s a demon. A curious boy approaches her and, over the course of a few days, she tells him two stories. Each of the two stories takes up about half of the book. Within each story, some of the characters tell other stories. Within those stories, somebody tells another story. These stories often tell the backstory of a particular character, so you’re sort of gaining more and more history, going backwards in time as you go forward in the book. Periodically, the book returns to the higher layers to continue those stories, and then it possibly goes back into the same lower layers to finish incomplete stories there, or else it starts a new inner story with a new set of layers. Some of the different branches were only moderately related, but there were lots of little connections here and there which were fun to watch for.<br /><br />Sound confusing? It really wasn’t. The first main story never went more than 5 layers deep. The second main story went up to 7 layers deep a couple times. When I first realized the structure of the book, I was a little worried that I would get confused, so I started checking myself each time the story went into a deeper layer, recounting to myself the steps that had led there. I was always able to do so quickly and without confusion, and I think that process helped me keep it all straight in my head. I could see where some people might find this book disorienting, though. For me, it may have helped that this type of thought process is part of my day job as a programmer; I kept making comparisons to it while I was reading. Reading this was kind of like keeping track of the call stack while reading or debugging a program as it progresses forward and backward through layers of subroutines. <br /><br />The stories all borrow heavily from fairy tales. This was especially noticeable to me since I had read through <i>The Complete Grimm’s Fairy Tales</i> earlier this year. It really isn’t a retelling of any of those stories, but there were lots of little nods, sometimes with similarities and sometimes with twists, and with the tiniest hint of satire. Unlike many of the Grimm’s tales, however, this book was internally consistent, the characters’ actions made sense, and it never felt silly. <br /><br />I do still have a little bit of Fairy Tale Fatigue from the Grimm’s book though, so that might have impacted my enjoyment of some of the stories. Some layers were more interesting than others, so the book didn’t always hold my interest, which is the main reason I’m not rating it higher. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17960570172398619578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_414578380" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/414578380" />
    <a title="Zach" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/428808-zach"><img alt="Zach" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536687522p2/428808.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/414578380?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zach" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zach" href="/user/show/428808-zach">Zach</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/428808-zach?shelf=feminism-gender">feminism-gender</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/428808-zach?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/428808-zach?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer414578380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2550501415519058234">One Thousand and One Nights meets European folktales and modern fantasy (think, perhaps, a somewhat more self-serious Princess Bride) in a nested series of linked short stories.* The overall frame, where a sultan's son is told the stories by an outcast orphan hiding on the palace grounds, is the least interesting part, but a good many of the other threads are incredibly effective, deftly examining and flipping gender roles, archetypes, tropes and cliches ("Never put your faith in a Prince. When </span>
  <span id="freeText2550501415519058234" style="display:none">One Thousand and One Nights meets European folktales and modern fantasy (think, perhaps, a somewhat more self-serious Princess Bride) in a nested series of linked short stories.* The overall frame, where a sultan's son is told the stories by an outcast orphan hiding on the palace grounds, is the least interesting part, but a good many of the other threads are incredibly effective, deftly examining and flipping gender roles, archetypes, tropes and cliches ("Never put your faith in a Prince. When you require a miracle, trust a Witch"). Particularly outstanding when dealing, as it often does, with melancholia and a deep sense of loss.<br /><br />The wide-ranging structure gives us a densely-built world without ever descending to rank infodumps, and there's a lot of of oblique self-referentialism and gamesmanship, if that's your sort of thing (and it is my sort of thing).<br /><br />All of this is told in prose so lush that it is at time downright sickening - I can understand why Valente was working in such baroque, vibrant strokes, but it was at times so over the top that it distracted from the content of the stories themselves. You have to be in a certain headspace for this, I think, but should also note that either she settles into a more natural approach as the book moves on, or else I just got used to the avalanche of similes.<br /><br />* As in: a prince (viewpoint #1) meets a witch (2) whose grandmother (3), when she was a girl, was taken in by a horsewoman (4), then we jump back to the grandmother (3) and then the prince (1), then return to the horsewoman's story (4) as she meets a wolf (5), and so on and so forth. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2550501415519058234" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1884490818" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1884490818?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="T.D. Whittle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="T.D. Whittle" href="/user/show/6051061-t-d-whittle">T.D. Whittle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6051061-t-d-whittle?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6051061-t-d-whittle?shelf=catherynne-valente">catherynne-valente</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1884490818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14586988234539779725">Marvelous, in the truest sense of the word. I am a Valente fan, my favourite of hers being <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3973532.Palimpsest' title='Palimpsest by Catherynne M. Valente' rel='nofollow noopener'>Palimpsest</a>, but also loving <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16146055.The_Melancholy_of_Mechagirl' title='The Melancholy of Mechagirl by Catherynne M. Valente' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Melancholy of Mechagirl</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8694389.Deathless__Leningrad_Diptych___1_' title='Deathless (Leningrad Diptych, #1) by Catherynne M. Valente' rel='nofollow noopener'>Deathless</a>, and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23453910.The_Fairyland_Series__Books_1_3_' title='The Fairyland Series (Books 1-3) by Catherynne M. Valente' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Fairyland Series</a>. I am loyal even to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18490533.Radiance' title='Radiance by Catherynne M. Valente' rel='nofollow noopener'>Radiance</a> because, although I could not engage with all of it, much of it I did, and its sense of place, mood, and imagery have stayed with me. <br/><br/>Like all of Valente's writing, <i>In the Night Garden</i> is metaphorically and visually evocative and potent. If you enjoyed <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7123161.The_Arabian_Nights_Tales_of_1001_Nights__Volume_1' title='The Arabian Nights Tales of 1001 Nights, Volume 1 by Anonymous' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Arabian Nights: Tales of 1001 </a></span>
  <span id="freeText14586988234539779725" style="display:none">Marvelous, in the truest sense of the word. I am a Valente fan, my favourite of hers being <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3973532.Palimpsest" title="Palimpsest by Catherynne M. Valente" rel="nofollow noopener">Palimpsest</a>, but also loving <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16146055.The_Melancholy_of_Mechagirl" title="The Melancholy of Mechagirl by Catherynne M. Valente" rel="nofollow noopener">The Melancholy of Mechagirl</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8694389.Deathless__Leningrad_Diptych___1_" title="Deathless (Leningrad Diptych, #1) by Catherynne M. Valente" rel="nofollow noopener">Deathless</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23453910.The_Fairyland_Series__Books_1_3_" title="The Fairyland Series (Books 1-3) by Catherynne M. Valente" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fairyland Series</a>. I am loyal even to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18490533.Radiance" title="Radiance by Catherynne M. Valente" rel="nofollow noopener">Radiance</a> because, although I could not engage with all of it, much of it I did, and its sense of place, mood, and imagery have stayed with me. <br /><br />Like all of Valente's writing, <i>In the Night Garden</i> is metaphorically and visually evocative and potent. If you enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7123161.The_Arabian_Nights_Tales_of_1001_Nights__Volume_1" title="The Arabian Nights Tales of 1001 Nights, Volume 1 by Anonymous" rel="nofollow noopener">The Arabian Nights: Tales of 1001 Nights, Volume 1</a>, then you will probably enjoy this book. It's similarly styled (the domineering sister in Night Garden is even named Dinarzhad) but with all of Valente's motifs and playfulness.</span>

<div id="review_1086714297" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1086714297" />
    <a title="gio" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23204207-gio"><img alt="gio" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597613414p2/23204207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1086714297?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="gio" class="user" itemprop="url" name="gio" href="/user/show/23204207-gio">gio</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1086714297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5569430223431975070"><b>“They were all whispers now, the two of them, conspirators and thieves."</b><br/><br/>Valente never disappoints. Such a marvelous writing and imagination.<br/><br/>Catherynne M. Valente is, in my opinion, one of the most talented fantasy author out there. Considering that In the night garden isn't one of her latest books, it's even more impressive. If I had to describe it I'd tell you that this is a matryoshka of stories. A story within a story whitin another story, a labyrinth in which it's easy to get lost. However i</span>
  <span id="freeText5569430223431975070" style="display:none"><b>“They were all whispers now, the two of them, conspirators and thieves."</b><br /><br />Valente never disappoints. Such a marvelous writing and imagination.<br /><br />Catherynne M. Valente is, in my opinion, one of the most talented fantasy author out there. Considering that In the night garden isn't one of her latest books, it's even more impressive. If I had to describe it I'd tell you that this is a matryoshka of stories. A story within a story whitin another story, a labyrinth in which it's easy to get lost. However it's extremely fascinating to see how all the storylines and their protagonists interweave. <br /><br />I don't think I can truly make this book justice with my words. Know this, In the night garden is clever, fascinating and a marvelous story about stories themselves. A book that focuses on storytelling itself. And in the end, dear reader, you can't help but ask yourself "Am I inside a story too?" </span>
  <a data-text-id="5569430223431975070" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TzopeFZMebjCxVPa9lt8/vbMM5uqVC9t35SpQOQH9NcomkrGnhJ6Ib1G2OYYOBDSg9TmQIJ0uXKOLzFS68qmeQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Xlomzox4DOlXJAvVrQPh6EEXxtq7BYE/b/SWJmX3Swg5+kVwRCYPcCingOlDYI3ENA8TAZMlFyA+Tw40ajoZpg==')})
  }

In an effort to retrieve his past, he withdraws to the family home somewhere in the hills between Milan and Turin. There, in the sprawling attic, he searches through boxes of old newspapers, comics, records, photo albums, and adolescent diaries. And so Yambo relives the story of his generation: Mussolini, Catholic education and guilt, Josephine Baker, Flash Gordon, Fred Astaire. His memories run wild, and the life racing before his eyes takes the form of a graphic novel. Yambo struggles through the frames to capture one simple, innocent image: that of his first love. <span id="freeTextContainer17675285291979861826">Catherynne M. Valente was born on Cinco de Mayo, 1979 in Seattle, WA, but grew up in in the wheatgrass paradise of Northern California. She graduated from high school at age 15, going on to UC San Diego and Edinburgh University, receiving her B.A. in Classics with an emphasis in Ancient Greek Linguistics. She then drifted away from her M.A. program and into a long residence in the concrete and cam</span>
  <span id="freeText17675285291979861826" style="display:none">Catherynne M. Valente was born on Cinco de Mayo, 1979 in Seattle, WA, but grew up in in the wheatgrass paradise of Northern California. She graduated from high school at age 15, going on to UC San Diego and Edinburgh University, receiving her B.A. in Classics with an emphasis in Ancient Greek Linguistics. She then drifted away from her M.A. program and into a long residence in the concrete and camphor wilds of Japan.<br /><br />She currently lives in Maine with her partner, two dogs, and three cats, having drifted back to America and the mythic frontier of the Midwest.</span>

And who can resist the stories she tells? From the Lake of the Dead and the City of Marrow to the artists who remain behind in a ghost city of spice, here are stories of hedgehog warriors and winged skeletons, loyal leopards and sparrow calligraphers. Nothing is too fantastic, anything can happen, but you’ll never guess what comes next in these intimately linked adventures of firebirds and djinn, singing manticores, mutilated unicorns, and women made entirely of glass and gears. Graced with the magical illustrations of Michael Kaluta, In the Cities of Coins and Spice is a book of dreams and wonders unlike any you’ve ever encountered.
